## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: The task models dA/dt as a function of concentration A and time t, which is the fundamental form of a rate law in chemical kinetics. The rate typically depends on powers of concentration, and time dependence may arise from coupled species, photochemical effects, or substituted analytical solutions.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order rate law: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order rate law: dA_dt = c0 * A (rate proportional to concentration)
- Second-order rate law: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (rate proportional to concentration squared)
- nth-order rate law: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law dependence on concentration)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse first-order reactions)
- Mixed-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (competing first and second order pathways)
- Michaelis-Menten / saturation kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A * c1 / (A + c2) (enzyme-catalyzed or surface reaction)
- Autocatalytic reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 + c2 * A) (product-catalyzed reaction)
- Logistic-type rate: dA_dt = c0 * A * (1 + c1 * A) (second-order with linear correction)
- Time-dependent first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (time-varying rate constant, e.g., temperature ramp)
- Coupled species substitution: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 + c2 * exp(c3 * t)) (rate involving another species expressed as function of time)
- Fractional order with time: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 * t (anomalous kinetics with drift)
- Product inhibition: dA_dt = c0 * A * c1 / (c2 + A**2) (substrate inhibition kinetics)
- Power-law with exponential decay: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 * exp(c2 * t) (combined concentration and time dependence)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Integer power of concentration → classical reaction order (1st, 2nd, 3rd order elementary reactions)
- Negative coefficient on A terms → consumption/decay of reactant species
- Rational function of A (numerator/denominator both involving A) → enzyme kinetics or surface-catalyzed Langmuir-Hinshelwood mechanism
- Product of A with (constant - A) → autocatalytic or logistic kinetics where total concentration is conserved
- Explicit time dependence multiplied by concentration → coupled reaction system where other species have been analytically eliminated
- Sum of two power-law terms in A → parallel competing reaction pathways with different orders
- Square root or fractional power of A → dissociative equilibrium or diffusion-limited kinetics
- A multiplied by exponential of negative t → reaction with a decaying catalyst or photodegradation with diminishing light source
- Polynomial in A with alternating signs → reversible reactions or equilibrium-approaching dynamics

This simplifies to: `c_a * A^(1/3) + c_b * A + c_c * A * exp(c_d * t)` where c_a ≈ 0.799, c_b ≈ -0.4995, c_c ≈ -0.4995, c_d ≈ -0.05057.

Key structural features:
- Term 1: `A^(1/3)` (power of A)
- Term 2: `A` (linear in A, constant in t)
- Term 3: `A * exp(negative * t)` (product of A and decaying exponential in t)

No terms with: sin, log, 1/(c+t)^2, A^3, A^5, etc. — unless those extra terms can be zeroed out.

Let me check candidates that have the right structure (A^c * c, A*c, and A*exp(c*t) or exp(c*t) terms):

I need to compare each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `0.79911*A^(1/3) - 0.49947*A - 0.49947*A*exp(-0.050570*t)`

This simplifies to: `c_a * A^(1/3) + c_b * A + c_c * A * exp(c_d * t)` where the key basis functions are:
- `A^(1/3)` (A to the power 1/3)
- `A` (linear in A)
- `A * exp(-k*t)` (A times a decaying exponential in t)

No constant offset, no standalone t terms, no sin terms, no log terms, etc.

Let me analyze each candidate systematically. For a match, the candidate must be able to express exactly these three basis functions and nothing else (extra terms must be zeroable).

**Key structural requirements:**
1. Must have `A^(c)` with c freely adjustable (to get A^(1/3))
2. Must have `A` term
3. Must have `A*exp(k*t)` term (or equivalent)
4. All other terms must be eliminable (set to zero)

The critical challenge: The GT has `A*exp(-k*t)` which is A multiplied by an exponential in t. Many candidates have `A/(c+t)^2` which is NOT equivalent to `A*exp(-kt)` — these are fundamentally different functions. Similarly, `A/sqrt(c+t)` is not `A*exp(-kt)`.

Let me check candidates that might have the right structure:

**Candidates with `A*exp(c*t)` type terms:**
- Candidates 8, 32, 33, 34, 40, 44: Have `A*c2` and `exp(c*t)` but the exponential is NOT multiplied by A. The GT needs `A*exp(...)`, not separate `exp(...)`.

**Candidate 31:** Has terms like `A*c0/(c1+t)` and `A^c2*c3*t/(c1+t)` etc. — complex rational structure, but no `A*exp(t)` term directly.

**Candidate 48:** `A*c0/(c1+t) + A*c1/(c1+t) + A*t/(c1+t) + c2*exp(A*c3)/(c1+t) + c4*exp(c5*t)/(c1+t) + c6*t*exp(A*c3)/(c1+t) + c7*t*exp(c5*t)/(c1+t)`

This has `exp(c5*t)/(c1+t)` terms but not `A*exp(t)`.

**Candidate 35:** `A*c0 + A*c1*(c2+t)^c3 + c4*t/(A*c5+c6) + c7/(A*c5+c6) + c8`

`A*(c2+t)^c3` — this is a power law in t, not exponential. NOT equivalent.

**Candidate 41:** `A*c0*(c1+t)^c2 + A*c3 + c4 + c5*exp(A*c6) + c7*t`

Again `A*(c1+t)^c2` is power law, not exponential. And `exp(A*c6)` is exponential in A, not t.

After careful review, **none** of the candidates contain the term `A*exp(c*t)` — they either have `exp(c*t)` without A multiplication, or `A/(c+t)^n` which is algebraic, not exponential. The GT fundamentally requires `A*exp(-k*t)` which cannot be replicated by any of these structural forms.

Let me verify each verdict:

Candidates 1-50: All lack the `A*exp(c*t)` basis function. The closest candidates have either `exp(c*t)` (not multiplied by A) or `A/(c+t)^2` (algebraic, not exponential). None can match.
